class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of Scottish monarchs</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about Scottish monarchs until 1707. For British monarchs since the Union of Scotland and England in 1707, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs" title="List of British monarchs">List of British monarchs</a>.</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Queen of Scots" redirects here. For the passenger train, see <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Scots_(train)" title="Queen of Scots (train)">Queen of Scots (train)</a>.</div>\n<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th style="text-align:center;background-color: #eee;"></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:MK18545_Bannockburn_Robert_the_Bruce.jpg" class="image"><img alt="MK18545 Bannockburn Robert the Bruce.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/MK18545_Bannockburn_Robert_the_Bruce.jpg/200px-MK18545_Bannockburn_Robert_the_Bruce.jpg" style="text-align:center;background-color: #eee;">Details</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">First&#160;monarch</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Kenneth_I_MacAlpin" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenneth I MacAlpin">Kenneth I MacAlpin</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Last&#160;monarch</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Anne</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Formation</th><td>\n843</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Abolition</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">1 May 1707</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg/300px-Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg.png" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg/450px-Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg/600px-Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Banner_of_Scotland.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Standard of Scotland">Royal Standard of the King of Scots</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>monarch of Scotland</b> was the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a>. According to tradition, the first <b>King of Scots</b> (<a href="/wiki/Middle_Scots" title="Middle Scots">Middle Scots</a>: <i>King of Scottis</i>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_Scots" title="Modern Scots">Modern Scots</a>: <i>King o Scots</i>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i>R\xc3\xacghrean Albannaich</i>) was <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_MacAlpin" title="Kenneth MacAlpin">Kenneth MacAlpin</a> (Cin\xc3\xa1ed mac Ailp\xc3\xadn), who founded the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">state</a> in 843. The distinction between the Kingdom of Scotland and the Kingdom of the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a> is rather the product of later medieval myth and confusion from a change in nomenclature i.e. <i>Rex Pictorum</i> (King of the Picts) becomes <i>R\xc3\xad Alban</i> (King of Alba) under <a href="/wiki/Donald_II_of_Scotland" title="Donald II of Scotland">Donald II</a> when annals switched from <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> to vernacular around the end of the 9th century, by which time the word Alba in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Gaelic</a> had come to refer to the Kingdom of the Picts rather than Great Britain (its older meaning).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_kings_of_the_Picts" title="List of kings of the Picts">Kingdom of the Picts</a> just became known as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Alba" title="Kingdom of Alba">Kingdom of Alba</a> in Gaelic, which later became known in <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a> and English as <i>Scotland</i>; the terms are retained in both languages to this day. By the late 11th century at the very latest, Scottish kings were using the term <i>rex Scottorum</i>, or King of Scots, to refer to themselves in Latin. The title of <i>King of Scots</i> fell out of use in 1707, when the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> was merged with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> to form a single <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>. Thus <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a> became the last monarch of the ancient kingdoms of Scotland and England and the first of Great Britain, although the kingdoms had shared a monarch since 1603 (see <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">Union of the Crowns</a>). Her uncle <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> was the last monarch to be <a href="/wiki/Coronations_in_Europe#Scotland" title="Coronations in Europe">crowned</a> in Scotland, at <a href="/wiki/Scone,_Perth_and_Kinross" class="mw-redirect" title="Scone, Perth and Kinross">Scone</a> in 1651. He had a second coronation in England ten years later.\n</p>\n<table class="vertical-navbox vcard" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px id="List_of_monarchs_of_Scotland">List of monarchs of Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: List of monarchs of Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Alpin_.28848.E2.80.931034.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Alpin_(848\xe2\x80\x931034)">House of Alpin (848\xe2\x80\x931034)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: House of Alpin (848\xe2\x80\x931034)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Kings_of_the_Picts" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Kings of the Picts">List of Kings of the Picts</a></div>\n<p>The reign of Kenneth MacAlpin begins what is often called the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Alpin" title="House of Alpin">House of Alpin</a>, an entirely modern concept. The descendants of Kenneth MacAlpin were divided into two branches; the crown would alternate between the two, the death of a king from one branch often hastened by war or assassination by a pretender from the other. Malcolm II was the last king of the House of Alpin; in his reign, he successfully crushed all opposition to him and, having no sons, was able to pass the crown to his daughter\'s son, Duncan I, who inaugurated the House of Dunkeld.\n</p>\n<table width="100%" class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="10%">Portrait\n</th>\n<th width="15%">Traditional modern English regnal name <br /><small>(with modern Gaelic equivalent)</small>\n</th>\n<th width="15%">Medieval Gaelic name\n</th>\n<th width="10%">Dynastic Status\n</th>\n<th width="10%">Reign\n</th>\n<th width="10%">Title\n</th>\n<th width="15%">Epithet\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kenneth MacAlpin.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg/99px-Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg" width="99" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg/148px-Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg/198px-Kenneth_MacAlpin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1057" data-file-height="1601" /></a>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><b><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_MacAlpin" title="Kenneth MacAlpin">Kenneth MacAlpin I</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><br /><small>(Coinneach mac Ailpein)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></small>\n</td>\n<td align="center">Cin\xc3\xa1ed mac Ailp\xc3\xadn<br />Ciniod m. mac Ailpein)</small>\n</td>\n<td align="center">Domnall mac Ailp\xc3\xadn\n</td>\n<td align="center">son of Alpin king of Dal Riata, and brother of Kenneth I\n</td>\n<td align="center">858 King. If he was, he was co-King with Giric. Amla\xc3\xadb is known only by a reference to his death in 977, which reports him as King of Alba; since Kenneth II is known to have still been King in 972\xe2\x80\x93973, Amla\xc3\xadb must have taken power between 973 and 977.\n</p><p>\xe2\x80\xa0 Eochiad was a son of Run, King of Strathclyde, but his mother was a daughter of Kenneth I.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Dunkeld_.281034.E2.80.931286.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Dunkeld_(1034\xe2\x80\x931286)">House of Dunkeld (1034\xe2\x80\x931286)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: House of Dunkeld (1034\xe2\x80\x931286)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Duncan succeeded to the throne as the maternal grandson of Malcolm II. He was also the heir-general of Malcolm I, as his paternal grandfather, Duncan of Atholl was the third son of Malcolm I. The House of Dunkeld was therefore closely related to the House of Alpin. Duncan was killed in battle by Macbeth, who had a long and relatively successful reign. In a series of battles between 1057 and 1058, Duncan\'s son Malcolm III defeated and killed Macbeth and Macbeth\'s stepson and heir Lulach, and claimed the throne. The dynastic feuds did not end there: on Malcolm\'s death in battle, his brother Donald Ban claimed the throne, expelling Malcolm\'s sons from Scotland; a civil war in the family ensued, with Donald Ban and Malcolm\'s son Edmund opposed by Malcolm\'s English-backed sons, led first by Duncan II and then by Edgar. Edgar triumphed, sending his uncle and brother to monasteries. After the reign of David I, the Scottish throne was passed according to rules of <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">primogeniture</a>, moving from father to son, or where not possible, brother to brother.\n</p>\n<table width="100%" class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="20%">Modern English &amp; Regnal Name<br /><small>(Modern Gaelic Name)<br />(Medieval Gaelic II\n</td>\n<td align="center">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Sverre_.281286.E2.80.931290.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Sverre_(1286\xe2\x80\x931290)">House of Sverre (1286\xe2\x80\x931290)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: House of Sverre (1286\xe2\x80\x931290)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/House_of_Sverre" title="House of Sverre">House of Sverre</a></div>\n<p>The last King of the House of Dunkeld was Alexander III. His wife had borne him two sons and a daughter; but by 1286 his sons were dead and his daughter, Margaret, had borne only a single daughter, also named Margaret, to her husband <a href="/wiki/Eric_II_of_Norway" title="Eric II of Norway">Eric II of Norway</a> before herself dying. Alexander had himself remarried, but in early 1286 he died in an accident while riding home. His wife, Yolande of Dreux, was pregnant; but by November 1286 all hope of her bearing a living child had passed. Accordingly, in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Salisbury" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Salisbury">Treaty of Salisbury</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guardians_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardians of Scotland">Guardians of Scotland</a> recognised Alexander\'s three-year-old granddaughter, Margaret of Norway, as Queen of Scots. Margaret remained in her father\'s Kingdom of Norway until Autumn 1290, when she was dispatched to Scotland. However, she died on the journey in Orkney, having never set foot on Scottish soil, and without being crowned at Scone. She is thus sometimes not considered Queen.\n</p>\n<table style="text-align:center; width:100%" class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name</th>\n<th>Portrait</th>\n<th>Birth</th>\n<th>Marriage(s)</th>\n<th>Death</th>\n<th>Dynastic status\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Margaret,_Maid_of_Norway" title="Margaret, Maid of Norway">Margaret</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><br /><i>the Maid of Norway</i><br />1286&#8211;1290</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:Margaret,_Maid_of_Norway_imaginary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Margaret, Maid of Norway imaginary.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Margaret%2C_Maid_of_Norway_imaginary.jpg/100px-Margaret%2C_Maid_of_Norway_imaginary.jpg" width="100" height="148" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Margaret%2C_Maid_of_Norway_imaginary.jpg/150px-Margaret%2C_Maid_of_Norway_imaginary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Margaret%2C_Maid_of_Norway_imaginary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="152" data-file-height="225" /></a></td>\n<td>c. April 1283<br /><a href="/wiki/T%C3%B8nsberg" title="T\xc3\xb8nsberg">T\xc3\xb8nsberg</a>, Norway<br />daughter of <a href="/wiki/Eric_II_of_Norway" title="Eric II of Norway">Eric II of Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_of_Scotland,_Queen_of_Norway" title="Margaret of Scotland, Queen of Norway">Margaret of Scotland</a></td>\n<td>unmarried</td>\n<td>September/October 1290<br /><a href="/wiki/St_Margaret%27s_Hope" title="St Margaret&#39;s Hope">St Margaret\'s Hope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a><br />aged 7</td>\n<td>granddaughter of Alexander III\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="First_Interregnum_.281290.E2.80.931292.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Interregnum_(1290\xe2\x80\x931292)">First Interregnum (1290\xe2\x80\x931292)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First Interregnum (1290\xe2\x80\x931292)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Guardian_of_Scotland" title="Guardian of Scotland">Guardian of Scotland</a></div>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Balliol_.281292.E2.80.931296.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Balliol_(1292\xe2\x80\x931296)">House of Balliol (1292\xe2\x80\x931296)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: House of Balliol (1292\xe2\x80\x931296)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The death of Margaret of Norway began a two-year interregnum in Scotland caused by a succession crisis. With her death, the descent of William I became extinct; nor was there an obvious heir by primogeniture. Thirteen candidates presented themselves; the most prominent were <a href="/wiki/John_Balliol" title="John Balliol">John de Balliol</a>, great-grandson of William I\'s younger brother David of Huntingdon, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_de_Brus,_5th_Lord_of_Annandale" title="Robert de Brus, 5th Lord of Annandale">Robert de Brus</a>, 5th Lord of <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Annandale" class="mw-redirect" title="Lordship of Annandale">Annandale</a>, David of Huntingdon\'s grandson. The Scottish Magnates invited <a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward I of England</a> to arbitrate the claims; he did so, but forced the Scots to swear allegiance to him as overlord. Eventually, it was decided that John de Balliol should become King; he proved weak and incapable, and in 1296 was forced to abdicate by Edward I, who then attempted to annex Scotland into the Kingdom of England.\n</p>\n<table style="text-align:center; width:100%" class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name</th>\n<th>Portrait</th>\n<th>Birth</th>\n<th>Marriage(s)</th>\n<th>Death</th>\n<th>Dynastic status\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/John_Balliol" title="John Balliol">John Balliol</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><br /><i>Toom Tabard</i> ("Empty Cloak")<br /><small>(Iain Balliol)</small><br />1292&#8211;1296</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:SetonArmorialJohnBalliolAndWife.jpg" class="image"><img 1249</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Isabella_de_Warenne" title="Isabella de Warenne">Isabella de Warenne</a><br />9 February 1281<br />at least one child</td>\n<td>\n<p>c. 25 November 1314<br /><a href="/wiki/Picardy" title="Picardy">Picardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td>great-grandson of <a href="/wiki/David_of_Scotland,_Earl_of_Huntingdon" class="mw-redirect" title="David of Scotland, Earl of Huntingdon">David</a> of <a href="/wiki/Earldom_of_Huntingdon" class="mw-redirect" title="Earldom of Huntingdon">Huntingdon</a> (brother of William I)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="Second_Interregnum_.281296.E2.80.931306.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Interregnum_(1296\xe2\x80\x931306)">Second Interregnum (1296\xe2\x80\x931306)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second Interregnum (1296\xe2\x80\x931306)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Guardian_of_Scotland" title="Guardian of Scotland">Guardian of Scotland</a></div>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Bruce_.281306.E2.80.931371.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Bruce_(1306\xe2\x80\x931371)">House of Bruce (1306\xe2\x80\x931371)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: House of Bruce (1306\xe2\x80\x931371)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For ten years, Scotland had no King of its own. The Scots, however, refused to tolerate English rule; first <a href="/wiki/William_Wallace" title="William Wallace">William Wallace</a> and then, after his execution, <a href="/wiki/Robert_the_Bruce" title="Robert the Bruce">Robert the Bruce</a> (the grandson of the 1292 competitor, Robert de Brus) fought against the English. Bruce and his supporters killed a rival for the throne, <a href="/wiki/John_III_Comyn,_Lord_of_Badenoch" title="John III Comyn, Lord of Badenoch">John III Comyn</a>, Lord of <a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Badenoch" class="mw-redirect" title="Lordship of Badenoch">Badenoch</a> on 10 February 1306 at Greyfriars Church in <a href="/wiki/Dumfries" title="Dumfries">Dumfries</a>. Shortly after in 1306, Robert was crowned King of Scots at Scone. His energy, and the corresponding replacement of the vigorous Edward I with his weaker son Edward II, allowed Scotland to free itself from English rule; at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bannockburn" title="Battle of Bannockburn">Battle of Bannockburn</a> in 1314, the Scots routed the English, and by 1328 the English had agreed by treaty to accept Scottish independence. Robert\'s son, David, acceded to the throne as a child. The English renewed their war with Scotland, and David was forced to flee the Kingdom by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Balliol" title="Edward Balliol">Edward Balliol</a>, son of King John, who managed to get himself crowned King of Scots (1332\xe2\x80\x931336) and to give away Scotland\'s southern counties to England before being driven out again. David spent much of his life in exile, first in freedom with his ally, France, and then in prison in England; he was only able to return to Scotland in 1357. Upon his death, childless, in 1371, the House of Bruce came to an end.\n</p>\n<table style="text-align:center; width:100%" Drummond, Queen of Scotland">Margaret Drummond</a><br />Inchmurdach, Fife<br />20 February 1364<br />no children</td>\n<td>22 February 1371<br /><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Castle" title="Edinburgh Castle">Edinburgh Castle</a><br />aged 46</td>\n<td>son of Robert I (<a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">primogeniture</a>)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<hr />\n<p><b>Disputed claimant</b>\n</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Edward_Balliol" title="Edward Balliol">Edward Balliol</a></b> was the son of King <a href="/wiki/John_Balliol" title="John Balliol">John Balliol</a>, who had himself ruled for four years following his election in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Cause" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Cause">Great Cause</a>.  Following his abdication, John Balliol lived out his life in obscurity in <a href="/wiki/Picardy" title="Picardy">Picardy</a>, France.  During the minority of David II, Edward Balliol seized the opportunity to assert his claim to the throne, and backed by the English, he defeated the forces of David\'s regency and was himself crowned king at <a href="/wiki/Scone" title="Scone">Scone</a> in 1332.  He was quickly defeated by loyalist forces, and sent back to England.  With English support, he would mount two more attempts to seize the throne again, in 1333 and 1335, each time his actual control of the throne was brief before being sent back to England, for the last time in 1336.  When David returned from exile in 1341 to rule in his own right, Edward lost most of his support.  When David II was captured in battle in 1346, Edward made one last attempt to seize the throne for himself, but had little support and the campaign fizzled before it gained much traction.  In 1356 he renounced all claims to the throne.\n</p>\n<table style="text-align:center; width:100%" exiled David II\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Stewart.2FStuart_.281371.E2.80.931651.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Stewart/Stuart_(1371\xe2\x80\x931651)">House of Stewart/Stuart (1371\xe2\x80\x931651)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: House of Stewart/Stuart (1371\xe2\x80\x931651)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/House_of_Stuart" title="House of Stuart">House of Stuart</a></div>\n<p>Robert the Stewart was a grandson of Robert I by the latter\'s daughter, Marjorie. Having been born in 1316, he was older than his uncle, David II; consequently, he was at his accession a middle aged man, already 55, and unable to reign vigorously, a problem also faced by his son Robert III, who also ascended in middle age at 53 in 1390, and suffered lasting damage in a horse-riding accident. These two were followed by a series of regencies, caused by the youth of the succeeding five boy kings. Consequently, the Stewart era saw periods of royal inertia, during which the nobles usurped power from the crown, followed by periods of personal rule by the monarch, during which he or she would attempt to address the issues created by their own minority and the long-term effects of previous reigns. Governing Scotland became increasingly difficult, as the powerful nobility became increasingly intractable; James I\'s attempts to curb the disorder of the realm ended in his assassination; James III was killed in a civil war between himself and the nobility, led by his own son; when James IV, who had governed sternly and suppressed the aristocrats, died in the Battle of Flodden, his wife Margaret Tudor, who had been nominated regent for their young son James V, was unseated by noble feuding, and James V\'s own wife, Mary of Guise, succeeded in ruling Scotland during the regency for her young daughter Mary I only by dividing and conquering the noble factions, and by distributing French bribes with a liberal hand. Finally, Mary I, the daughter of James V, found herself unable to govern Scotland faced with the surliness of the aristocracy and the intransigence of the population, who favoured Calvinism and disapproved of her Catholicism; she was forced to abdicate, and fled to England, where she was imprisoned in various castles and manor houses for eighteen years and finally executed for treason against the English queen Elizabeth I. Upon her abdication, her son, fathered by <a href="/wiki/Henry,_Lord_Darnley" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry, Lord Darnley">Henry, Lord Darnley</a>, a junior member of the Stewart family, became King as James VI.\n</p><p>James VI became King of England and Ireland as James I in 1603, when his cousin Elizabeth I died; thereafter, although the two crowns of England and Scotland remained separate, the monarchy was based chiefly in England. Charles I, James\'s son, found himself faced with Civil War; the resultant conflict lasted eight years, and ended in his execution. The English Parliament then decreed their monarchy to be at an end; the Scots Parliament, after some deliberation, broke their links with England, and declared that Charles II, son and heir of Charles I, would become King. He ruled until 1651 when the armies of <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> occupied Scotland and drove him into exile.\n</p>\n<table style="text-align:center; width:100%" class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name</th>\n<th>Portrait</th>\n<th>Birth</th>\n<th>Marriage(s)</th>\n<th>Death</th>\n<th>Dynastic status\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a (1651\xe2\x80\x931660)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Third Interregnum (1651\xe2\x80\x931660)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scotland_under_the_Commonwealth" title="Scotland under the Commonwealth">Scotland under the Commonwealth</a></div>\n<h3><span id="House_of_Stuart_restored_.281660.E2.80.931707.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Stuart_restored_(1660\xe2\x80\x931707)">House of Stuart restored (1660\xe2\x80\x931707)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: House of Stuart restored (1660\xe2\x80\x931707)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Restoration">Scottish Restoration</a>, the Stuarts became Kings of Scotland once more. But Scotland\'s rights were not respected: the Scottish Parliament was, during the reign of Charles II, dissolved, and his brother <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James</a> was appointed Governor of Scotland. James himself became James VII in 1685; his Catholicism was not tolerated, and he was driven out of England after three years. In his place came his daughter Mary and her husband William of Orange, the ruler of the Dutch Republic; they were accepted as monarchs of Scotland after a period of deliberation by the Scottish Parliament, and ruled together as William II and Mary II.\n</p><p>An attempt to establish a Scottish colonial empire through the <a href="/wiki/Darien_Scheme" class="mw-redirect" title="Darien Scheme">Darien Scheme</a>, in rivalry to that of England, failed, leaving the Scottish nobles who financed the venture for their own profit bankrupt. This coincided with the accession of <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a>, daughter of James VII. Anne had multiple children but none of these survived her, leaving as her heir her half-brother, James, then living in exile in France. The English favoured the Protestant Sophia of Hanover (a granddaughter of James VI) as heir; many Scots preferred Prince James, who as a Stuart was a Scot by ancestry, and threatened to break the Union of Crowns between England and Scotland by choosing him for themselves. To preserve the union, the English elaborated a plan whereby the two Kingdoms of Scotland and England would merge into a single Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>, ruled by a common monarch, and with a single Parliament. Both national parliaments agreed to this (the Scots albeit reluctantly, motivated primarily by the national finances), and some subterfuge as a total majority of signatories was needed to ratify the Scottish parliament\'s assent, bribes and payments. Thereafter, although monarchs continued to rule over the nation of Scotland, they did so first as <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs" title="List of British monarchs">monarchs of Great Britain</a>, and from 1801 of the United Kingdom.\n</p>\n<table style="text-align:center; width:100%" <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs" title="List of British monarchs">List of British monarchs</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jacobite_claimants">Jacobite claimants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Jacobite claimants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_succession" title="Jacobite succession">Jacobite succession</a></div>\n<p>James VII continued to claim the thrones of England, Scotland, and Ireland. When he died in 1701, his son James inherited his father\'s claims, and called himself James VIII of Scotland and III of England and Ireland. He would continue to do so all his life, even after the Kingdoms of England and Scotland were ended by their merging as the Kingdom of Great Britain. In 1715, a year after the death of his sister, Queen Anne, and the accession of their cousin George of Hanover, James landed in Scotland and attempted to claim the throne; he failed, and was forced to flee back to the Continent. A second attempt by his son, Charles on behalf of his father, in 1745, also failed. Both James\'s children died without legitimate issue, bringing the Stuart family to an end.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Francis_Edward_Stuart" title="James Francis Edward Stuart">James VIII</a> (Seumas VIII), also known as <i>The Old Pretender</i>, son of James VII, was claimant from 1701 until his death in 1766.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles III</a> (Te\xc3\xa0rlach III), also known as <i>The Young Pretender</i> and often called <i>Bonnie Prince Charlie</i>, son of James VIII, was claimant from his father\'s death until his own death in 1788 without legitimate issue.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Benedict_Stuart" title="Henry Benedict Stuart">Henry I</a> (Eanraig I), brother of Charles III and youngest son of James VIII. Died unmarried in 1807.</li></ul>\n<p>After 1807, the Jacobite claims passed first to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Savoy" title="House of Savoy">House of Savoy</a> (1807\xe2\x80\x931840), then to the Modenese branch of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">House of Habsburg-Lorraine</a> (1840\xe2\x80\x931919), and finally to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wittelsbach" title="House of Wittelsbach">House of Wittelsbach</a> (since 1919). The current heir is <a href="/wiki/Franz,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Franz, Duke of Bavaria">Franz</a>, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Bavaria</a>.  Neither he nor any of his predecessors since 1807 have pursued their claim.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline_of_Scottish_Monarchs">Timeline of Scottish Monarchs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Timeline of Scottish Monarchs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_66e344b4d43e29efff5cb4beceac9a10"><area shape="rect" alt="House of Alpin" /></map><img usemap="#timeline_66e344b4d43e29efff5cb4beceac9a10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/66e344b4d43e29efff5cb4beceac9a10.png" /></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acts_of_Union">Acts of Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Acts of Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs" title="List of British monarchs">List of British monarchs</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a> were twin <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Parliamentary Acts</a> passed during 1706 and 1707 by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_England" title="Parliament of England">Parliament of England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a>, putting into effect the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union" title="Treaty of Union">Treaty of Union</a>, agreed on 22 July 1706, following prolonged negotiation between Queen Anne\'s Commissioners representing both parliaments. The Acts joined the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> to form a united <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland and England had shared a common monarch since the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">Union of the Crowns</a> in 1603, when <a href="/wiki/King_James_VI_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="King James VI of Scotland">James VI, King of Scots</a>, inherited the English throne from his first cousin twice removed, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth I of England">Queen Elizabeth I of England</a>. Although described as a Union of Crowns, prior to the Acts of Union of 1707, the crowns of the two separate kingdoms had rested on the same head. Three unsuccessful attempts (in 1606, 1667, and 1689) were made to unite the two kingdoms by Acts of Parliament, but it was not until the early 18th century that the idea had the will of both political establishments to succeed, thereby bringing the two separate states together under a single parliament as well as a single monarch.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coronation_Oath">Coronation Oath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Coronation Oath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Coronation Oath was sworn by every King of Scots from <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">James VI</a> to <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> and approved by the <a href="/wiki/Estates_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Estates of Parliament">Estates of Parliament</a> in 1567:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>I, N.N., promise faithfully, in the presence of the eternal, my God, that I, enduring the whole Course of my Life, shall serve the same Eternal, my God, to the utmost of my Power, accordingly as he required in his most Holy Word, revealed and contained in the New and <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>; and according to the same Word shall maintain the true Religion of Jesus Christ, the preaching of his Holy Word, and due and right administration of his <a href="/wiki/Sacrament" title="Sacrament">Sacraments</a>, now received and practised within this Realm; and shall abolish and oppose all false Religion contrary to the same; and shall rule the People committed to my Charge, according to the Will and Command of God, revealed in his foresaid Word, and according to the lovable Laws and Constitutions received in this Realm, in no way repugnant to the said Word of the Eternal, my God; and shall procure to my utmost to the <a href="/wiki/Kirk" title="Kirk">Kirk</a> of God and whole Christian people true and perfect Peace in all times coming; the Rights and Rents, with all just privileges of the Crown of Scotland, I shall preserve and keep inviolate, neither shall I transfer nor alienate the same; I shall forbid and repress in all Estates and all Degrees theft, Oppression and all kind of Wrong; in all Judgements, I shall command and procure that Justice and Equity be kept to all creatures without exception, as he be merciful to me and you that is the Lord and Father of all Mercies; and out of all my lands and empire I shall be careful to root out all <a href="/wiki/Heresy" title="Heresy">Heresy</a> and Enemies to the true Worship of God, that shall be convicted by the true Kirk of God of the foresaid Crimes; and these Things above-written I faithfully affirm by my solemn Oath.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The Coronation Oath sworn by <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_II_of_England" title="Mary II of England">Mary II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Anne</a> was approved by the Parliament of Scotland on 18 April 1689.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The oath was as follows:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>WE William and Mary, King and Queen of Scotland, faithfully promise and swear, by this our solemn Oath, in presence of the Eternal God, that during the whole Course of our Life we will serve the same Eternal God, to the uttermost of our Power, according as he has required in his most Holy Word, revealed and contained in the New and Old Testament; and according to the same Word shall maintain the true Religion of Christ Jesus, the preaching of his Holy Word, and the due and right Ministration of the Sacraments, now received and preached within the Realm of Scotland; and shall abolish and gainstand all false Religion contrary to the same, and shall rule the People committed to our Charge, according to the Will and Command of God, revealed in his aforesaid Word, and according to the laudable Laws and Constitutions received in this Realm, no ways repugnant to the said Word of the Eternal God; and shall procure, to the utmost of our power, to the Kirk of God, and whole Christian People, true and perfect Peace in all time coming. That we shall preserve and keep inviolated the Rights and Rents, with all just Privileges of the Crown of Scotland, neither shall we transfer nor alienate the same; that we shall forbid and repress in all Estates and Degrees, Reif, Oppression and all kind of Wrong. And we shall command and procure, that Justice and Equity in all Judgments be kept to all Persons without exception, us the Lord and Father of all Mercies shall be merciful to us. And we shall be careful to root out all Heretics and Enemies to the true Worship of God, that shall be convicted by the true Kirk of God, of the aforesaid Crimes, out of our Lands and Empire of Scotland. And we faithfully affirm the Things above-written by our solemn Oath.</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Scottish_monarchs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span
